reference PyTorch source (the prompt the agent sees)
import torch
import torch.nn as nn

class Model(nn.Module):
    """
    Simple model that performs a convolution, applies Mish, and another Mish.
    """
    def __init__(self, in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size):
        super(Model, self).__init__()
        self.conv = nn.Conv2d(in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size)

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.conv(x)
        x = torch.nn.functional.mish(x)
        x = torch.nn.functional.mish(x)
        return x

batch_size   = 64  
in_channels  = 64  
out_channels = 128  
height = width = 256
kernel_size = 3

def get_inputs():
    return [torch.rand(batch_size, in_channels, height, width)]

def get_init_inputs():
    return [in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size]

We need to write a custom CUDA kernel that implements Conv2d + Mish + Mish. The reference does a conv2d (presumably with bias? nn.Conv2d default bias=True) then mish then mish. We need to fuse these operations into a single CUDA kernel to be faster. We need to handle the convolution ourselves. Since kernel_size=3, in_channels=64, out_channels=128, input 256x256, batch=64. That's a fairly large convolution. Fusing a 3x3 conv + mish + mish into a single kernel may be challenging because conv2d is usually implemented with cuDNN highly optimized. However, maybe we can use Winograd or im2col + GEMM? But writing a highly optimized conv from scratch might not beat cuDNN. However, the reference does two separate elementwise mish ops after conv, which are memory-bound. A fused kernel that computes conv + mish + mish in one pass could reduce memory bandwidth, potentially speeding up overall. But cuDNN conv might be very fast, and fusing elementwise ops after it may have small overhead. The custom kernel might be slower if conv implementation is naive. We need to think carefully. We need to produce a CUDA kernel using torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline. We could implement conv as a GEMM using im2col in shared memory and then apply mish. But for 3x3 conv, there might be a more direct approach: each thread block computes a tile of output channels and spatial locations, loading a corresponding input tile into shared memory, applying the filter, accumulating, then applying mish twice. Given the sizes: batch 64, in_channels 64, out_channels 128, H=W=256. The total output elements = 64*128*256*256 = 536,870,912. That's a lot. Each output is computed by 64*3*3 = 576 multiply-adds. So total FLOPs ~ 309 GFLOPs. Memory for output: 536M * 4 bytes = 2.1 GB. Input: 64*64*256*256 = 268M *4 = 1.07 GB. Weights: 128*64*3*3 = 73,728 *4 = 0.3 MB. Bias: 128*4 = 512 B. The reference: conv (reads input + weights, writes output), then mish (reads output, writes output), then mish (reads output, writes output). So total memory traffic: input 1.07GB + weights negligible + output written 3 times (conv out, mish1 out, mish2 out) + output read 2 times (mish1 read, mish2 read) = ~1.07 + 5*2.1 = 11.6 GB. At ~1-2 TB/s bandwidth, that's ~6-12 ms. Compute ~309 GFLOPs on GPU maybe 0.3 ms if compute bound. So overall time is memory bound. Fusing everything into one kernel that reads input once, writes output once would reduce memory to ~1.07 + 2.1 = 3.2 GB, ~3x speedup potential. So writing a fused conv+mish+mish kernel is likely beneficial even if conv is not as optimized as cuDNN, because memory bound dominates. However, cuDNN conv is very efficient, maybe much faster than naive conv, but still memory bound for the subsequent mish ops. But if cuDNN conv is highly optimized (e.g., using implicit GEMM with good shared memory usage), the time for conv might be ~1-2 ms. Then two mish elementwise ops on 2GB each might be ~2-4 ms. We can use compile-time constants for tile sizes to maximize performance. Let's define: ``` constexpr int TILE_H = 8; constexpr int TILE_W = 8; constexpr int TILE_OC = 16; constexpr int KH = 3; constexpr int KW = 3; ``` Shared memory: ``` __shared__ float s_in[TILE_H + KH - 1][TILE_W + KW - 1]; __shared__ float s_w[TILE_OC][KH][KW]; ``` Each block computes a tile of output. Compute base coordinates: ``` int n = blockIdx.z / ((C_out + TILE_OC - 1) / TILE_OC); int oc_tile = blockIdx.z % ((C_out + TILE_OC - 1) / TILE_OC); int oc_base = oc_tile * TILE_OC; int oc = oc_base + threadIdx.z; int h_base = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int w_base = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int h_out = h_base + threadIdx.y; int w_out = w_base + threadIdx.x; ``` Need to handle case where oc >= C_out, or h_out >= H_out, w_out >= W_out. We'll mask writes. Load input patch: Input dimensions: [N, C_in, H, W]. For a given channel c, offset = ((n * C_in + c) * H + h) * W + w. We load `s_in[i][j]` for i in [0, TILE_H+KH-2], j in [0, TILE_W+KW-2]. That's (8+2)*(8+2) = 10x10 = 100 elements. We need to load them collaboratively. Let's assign a linear thread id `int tid = threadIdx.z * TILE_H * TILE_W + threadIdx.y * TILE_W + threadIdx.x;` which ranges 0..1023. Then: ``` int patch_size = (TILE_H + KH - 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1); // 100 if (tid < patch_size) { int pi = tid / (TILE_W + KW - 1); int pj = tid % (TILE_W + KW - 1); int h_in = h_base + pi; int w_in = w_base + pj; float val = 0.0f; if (h_in >= 0 && h_in < H && w_in >= 0 && w_in < W) { val = input[((n * C_in + c) * H + h_in) * W + w_in]; } s_in[pi][pj] = val; } ``` Wait, h_base = blockIdx.y * TILE_H. Since blockIdx.y >= 0, h_in >= 0 always. But w_in similarly. However, for general case with padding, we could allow negative, but here no padding. So `if (h_in < H && w_in < W)` is enough. But for the last tile, h_base + pi may be up to 248+9 = 257 > 255 (since H=256). So need `h_in < H`. Good. Loading weights: ``` if (tid < TILE_OC * KH * KW) { int tz = tid / (KH * KW); int tky = (tid % (KH * KW)) / KW; int tkx = tid % KW; int oc_idx = oc_base + tz; float val = 0.0f; if (oc_idx < C_out) { val = weight[((oc_idx * C_in + c) * KH + tky) * KW + tkx]; } s_w[tz][tky][tkx] = val; } ``` But we need to load weights for each channel c inside the loop. Since `c` varies, the weight address changes, but we can compute with c. However, note that `s_w` size is `[TILE_OC][KH][KW]`. If `tid` goes up to 1023, and `TILE_OC*KH*KW` = 16*3*3 = 144, then first 144 threads load weights. That's fine. Then __syncthreads(); Now compute: ``` float acc = 0.0f; if (oc < C_out && h_out < H_out && w_out < W_out) { #pragma unroll for (int ky = 0; ky < KH; ++ky) { #pragma unroll for (int kx = 0; kx < KW; ++kx) { float iv = s_in[threadIdx.y + ky][threadIdx.x + kx]; float wv = s_w[threadIdx.z][ky][kx]; acc += iv * wv; } } } ``` Wait, `s_w` indexing: threadIdx.z is 0..15. For threads where `oc >= C_out`, `threadIdx.z` may map to an out-of-bounds channel. But `s_w` for those z's would have been loaded with 0 if oc_idx >= C_out. So `acc` would be 0. However, we only care about valid threads. Using `s_w[threadIdx.z]` is fine as long as we loaded zeros for invalid channels. But if `oc >= C_out`, we don't need to compute at all. We can guard: ``` if (oc < C_out && h_out < H_out && w_out < W_out) { // compute } ``` Inside this guard, `threadIdx.z < TILE_OC` and `oc_base + threadIdx.z < C_out`. Since `oc_base` is multiple of TILE_OC, and last tile might have fewer than TILE_OC valid channels. For `oc_base + threadIdx.z >= C_out`, we would not enter the compute block, but other threads in the warp might. This causes divergence within warp, but only at the boundary, and only for the last out_ch tile (which is 1 out of 8). So minimal divergence. Similarly for spatial boundaries: h_out and w_out. Since tile sizes divide almost evenly (254 not divisible by 8), some threads on edges are invalid. Divergence at boundaries. Now accumulation across input channels. We need either a local accumulator `float acc = 0.0f;` inside the `c` loop: ``` float acc = 0.0f; for (int c = 0; c < C_in; ++c) { // load input patch for channel c // load weights for channel c // __syncthreads() if (valid) { // dot product } __syncthreads() } ``` This requires `acc` to persist across the loop. That's fine. After the loop, if valid: ``` acc += bias[oc]; float v = mish(acc); v = mish(v); output[((n * C_out + oc) * H_out + h_out) * W_out + w_out] = v; ``` Implement `mish`: ``` __device__ __forceinline__ float mish(float x) { float sp; if (x > 0.0f) { sp = x + log1pf(expf(-x)); } else { sp = log1pf(expf(x)); } return x * tanhf(sp); } ``` But for fp32, `log1pf` is available? In CUDA C, `log1pf` is a device function. Yes. `expf`, `tanhf` are also available. We need to be careful: after first mish, we apply mish again. Compute: ``` float v = mish(acc + bias[oc]); v = mish(v); ``` Alternatively, we could fuse bias into acc first. Potential issue: When x is large negative, expf(x) underflows to 0, log1pf(0) = 0, so sp=0, mish = x * tanh(0) = 0. That matches limit. When x is large positive, expf(-x) underflows to 0, log1pf(0)=0, sp=x, tanh(x)→1, mish→x. So stable. This implementation is exact and safe. Now, we need to think about performance. The kernel will be memory-bound due to reading input. But can we achieve good memory throughput? Input loads: each block loads 100 floats per input channel. With 64 channels, that's 6400 floats = 25.6 KB per block. With ~1024 threads, each thread loads on average ~6.25 floats for input. But we only have 100 threads doing loads. For a given channel c, the input patch memory layout is row-major. 100 threads loading 100 contiguous floats? Let's see: input offset for h_in, w_in is `((n*C_in + c)*H + h_in)*W + w_in`. Then `&s_in[ty][tx]` = base + ty*patchW + tx. For threads with varying tx but same ty, addresses are consecutive. In our warp, there are groups of 8 threads with same y and varying x. But then next group has y+1. So 8 threads have consecutive addresses, then a gap of patchW-8 = 2 to next group. This is not bad. For a warp, it accesses 32 floats. They span 4 rows (y=0..3). Each row has 8 floats contiguous. So there are 4 segments of 8 contiguous floats. The hardware can handle this with 4 shared memory transactions. That's okay. Could be better to have threads load transposed or use different block shape (e.g., x=spatial, y=out_ch?). But let's keep it simple. Let's test compile and correctness. One more thing: We need to handle dynamic shapes but the kernel can be generic with template parameters for TILE sizes. We'll define them as macros or constants. Also, we need to handle the case where output dimensions are not aligned. We used `valid` to guard writes. Inside `if(valid)`, we compute convolution. But the `__syncthreads()` at the end of loop requires all threads in block to reach it. Since `valid` threads are a subset, but `__syncthreads()` is outside the `if(valid)`. In our code, `__syncthreads()` is placed unconditionally at the end of the loop body, after the compute `if(valid)`. So all threads will call `__syncthreads()`. Good. However, the compute `if(valid)` is inside the loop, so invalid threads do not read shared memory. Is that okay? Yes, because all threads in block will call `__syncthreads()`; invalid threads simply skip the reads. Since `__syncthreads()` ensures all threads have finished using shared memory before the next iteration overwrites it, it's safe. The only issue is if there are threads that are invalid and don't participate in the compute, but they still participate in syncthreads. That's fine. But note: if `oc >= C_out`, the thread doesn't need to compute. However, other threads in the block (same x,y, different z) might need `s_w[ky][kx][threadIdx.z]` where threadIdx.z is for a valid oc. The `s_w` is written for all tz. For invalid tz, we loaded 0. So if invalid thread tries to read `s_w` in compute (but we guard with `valid`, so it doesn't). So safe. One more thing: For the last block in a dimension, some threads are spatially invalid (h_out >= H_out or w_out >= W_out). They don't compute and don't write. The shared memory `s_in` is loaded for the entire patch regardless. The load uses `if (h_in < H && w_in < W)`. For out-of-bounds, loads 0. So compute for spatially invalid threads would be zero, but they are skipped. That's fine. Potential risk: If we use `s_in[threadIdx.y + ky][threadIdx.x + kx]` inside `if(valid)`, but threadIdx.y + ky can be up to 7+2=9, which is within 10. So okay. Now, launch config: Need to compute `num_oc_tiles = (C_out + TILE_OC - 1) / TILE_OC;` `dim3 grid((W_out + TILE_W - 1) / TILE_W, (H_out + TILE_H - 1) / TILE_H, N * num_oc_tiles);` `dim3 block(TILE_W, TILE_H, TILE_OC);` Need to ensure grid.z doesn't exceed 65535. Here N=64, num_oc_tiles=8, grid.z=512. Fine. Now, what about register usage? Each thread has `acc` (1 register), plus `v`, plus loop indices. Very low. So occupancy is max. Let's check if `input`, `weight`, `bias`, `output` pointers are `float*`. We assume fp32. The reference uses fp32 by default (torch.rand gives fp32). ModelNew should accept same args. The reference does `self.conv = nn.Conv2d(...)`. So our init is same. We need to define the CUDA source as a string in Python and call `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline`. The module loading time is at import time, acceptable. Important: `load_inline` caches based on source hash. The function names must be listed in `functions=[...]`. We will define a C++ function `fused_conv_mish_mish_forward` that launches the kernel. We must not include `PYBIND11_MODULE`. Let's draft the code. CUDA source: ``` #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #define TILE_H 8 #define TILE_W 8 #define TILE_OC 16 #define KH 3 #define KW 3 __device__ __forceinline__ float mish(float x) { float sp; if (x > 0.0f) { sp = x + log1pf(expf(-x)); } else { sp = log1pf(expf(x)); } return x * tanhf(sp); } __global__ void fused_conv_mish_mish_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ bias, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C_in, int H, int W, int C_out, int H_out, int W_out) { int num_oc_tiles = (C_out + TILE_OC - 1) / TILE_OC; int n = blockIdx.z / num_oc_tiles; int oc_tile = blockIdx.z % num_oc_tiles; int oc_base = oc_tile * TILE_OC; int oc = oc_base + threadIdx.z; int h_base = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int w_base = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int h_out = h_base + threadIdx.y; int w_out = w_base + threadIdx.x; bool valid = (n < N) && (oc < C_out) && (h_out < H_out) && (w_out < W_out); __shared__ float s_in[TILE_H + KH - 1][TILE_W + KW - 1]; __shared__ float s_w[KH][KW][TILE_OC]; int patchH = TILE_H + KH - 1; int patchW = TILE_W + KW - 1; int patchSize = patchH * patchW; int wTileSize = KH * KW * TILE_OC; float acc = 0.0f; const int tid = threadIdx.z * (TILE_H * TILE_W) + threadIdx.y * TILE_W + threadIdx.x; for (int c = 0; c < C_in; ++c) { // load input patch if (tid < patchSize) { int pi = tid / patchW; int pj = tid % patchW; int h_in = h_base + pi; int w_in = w_base + pj; float val = 0.0f; if (h_in < H && w_in < W) { val = input[((n * C_in + c) * H + h_in) * W + w_in]; } s_in[pi][pj] = val; } // load weights for this channel and output tile if (tid < wTileSize) { int tz = tid % TILE_OC; int tky = (tid / TILE_OC) / KW; int tkx = (tid / TILE_OC) % KW; int oc_idx = oc_base + tz; float val = 0.0f; if (oc_idx < C_out) { val = weight[((oc_idx * C_in + c) * KH + tky) * KW + tkx]; } s_w[tky][tkx][tz] = val; } __syncthreads(); if (valid) { #pragma unroll for (int ky = 0; ky < KH; ++ky) { #pragma unroll for (int kx = 0; kx < KW; ++kx) { float iv = s_in[threadIdx.y + ky][threadIdx.x + kx]; float wv = s_w[ky][kx][threadIdx.z]; acc += iv * wv; } } } __syncthreads(); } if (valid) { acc += bias[oc]; float v = mish(acc); v = mish(v); output[((n * C_out + oc) * H_out + h_out) * W_out + w_out] = v; } } torch::Tensor fused_conv_mish_mish_forward( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias) { int N = input.size(0); int C_in = input.size(1); int H = input.size(2); int W = input.size(3); int C_out = weight.size(0); int H_out = H - weight.size(2) + 1; int W_out = W - weight.size(3) + 1; auto output = torch::empty({N, C_out, H_out, W_out}, input.options()); dim3 block(TILE_W, TILE_H, TILE_OC); int num_oc_tiles = (C_out + TILE_OC - 1) / TILE_OC; dim3 grid( (W_out + TILE_W - 1) / TILE_W, (H_out + TILE_H - 1) / TILE_H, N * num_oc_tiles ); fused_conv_mish_mish_kernel<<<grid, block>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), N, C_in, H, W, C_out, H_out, W_out ); return output; } ``` We need to ensure that `bias` is not None. `nn.Conv2d` default bias=True. So bias exists. But we can handle None if needed. Wait: we need to import `torch` and define `ModelNew`. Let's write the Python code. ``` import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline cuda_source = r''' ... C++ code ... ''' cpp_source = r''' torch::Tensor fused_conv_mish_mish_forward(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias); ''' # Actually load_inline expects cpp_sources and cuda_sources fused_conv = load_inline( name='fused_conv_mish_mish', cpp_sources=cpp_source, cuda_sources=cuda_source, functions=['fused_conv_mish_mish_forward'], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3', '--use_fast_math'], verbose=False, ) ``` Wait, `cpp_sources` should contain the C++ wrapper. Given time, we will assert kernel_size == 3. Now, let's think about correctness of mish. Mish: `x * tanh(softplus(x))`. Our implementation: ``` if (x > 0.0f) sp = x + log1pf(expf(-x)); else sp = log1pf(expf(x)); return x * tanhf(sp); ``` Is this equivalent to PyTorch's mish? PyTorch's mish uses: ``` fused_mish = x * torch.tanh(F.softplus(x, beta=1.0, threshold=20.0)) ``` Wait, PyTorch `torch.nn.functional.mish(x)` probably uses a numerically stable implementation. Let's check typical CUDA implementation of mish in PyTorch: ``` template <typename T> __device__ T mish(T x) { return x * tanh(softplus(x)); } ``` And `softplus` is likely `log1p(exp(x))` with a cutoff: `x > 20 ? x : log1p(exp(x))` or something. Actually PyTorch's softplus with default beta=1 and threshold=20 is: ``` float sp = (x > threshold) ? x : log1p(exp(x)); ``` But `log1p(exp(x))` for x > 20 is numerically close to x. However, PyTorch's mish might be implemented similarly to ours? Let's verify by examining PyTorch source. PyTorch's `mish` CUDA kernel (ATen/native/cuda/Activation.cu) likely: ``` __device__ scalar_t mish(scalar_t x) { return x * tanh(softplus(x)); } ``` And `softplus` is defined elsewhere. In PyTorch, `mish` used to be implemented as `x * tanh(softplus(x))` where `softplus` uses a custom formula. But for fp32, the difference between using `log1pf(expf(x))` directly vs thresholding is small for typical values. However, for large x, `expf(x)` overflows for x > ~88.6. In our case, x after conv could be large? Weights are Kaiming uniform (~1/24), inputs are 0..1, sum of 64*3*3 terms plus bias. Bias is uniform(-sqrt(k), sqrt(k)), where k=1/(in_ch*kh*kw). So bias ~ ±1/24. The sum of 576 terms each ~1/24 ≈ 24. So outputs could be around ±24 or more if random. `expf(24)` is huge but not overflow (~2.6e10). `expf(88)` overflows. So our values are well within safe range. Actually outputs could be as large as sum of all positive maxima: input max 1, weight max maybe ~0.05. Sum ≈ 576*0.05 = 28.8. Bias ~0.05. So typical max ~30. `expf(30)` is ~1e13, safe. So using `expf` directly is safe. The threshold of 20 is for numerical stability but not strictly necessary for correctness. The difference for x>20 is tiny: `log1pf(expf(x))` ≈ x + exp(-x) (since log1p(y) ≈ log(y) for large y, but more precisely log1p(e^x) = log(1+e^x) = x + log(1+e^{-x}) = x + log1p(e^{-x}). For x>20, e^{-x} is very small, log1p(e^{-x}) ≈ e^{-x}. So `sp = x + tiny`. Then tanh(sp) ≈ tanh(x) ≈ 1 - 2e^{-2x}. `tanhf` for large x returns 1.0. So the product is x*1.0 = x. If we compute `sp = x + log1pf(expf(-x))`, for x=20, exp(-20) is ~2e-9, log1pf(2e-9) ≈ 2e-9, sp ≈ 20.000000002, tanh ≈ 1 (float precision), mish ≈ 20. So safe. If we computed `sp = log1pf(expf(x))` for x=20, exp(20) = 4.85e8, log1pf(4.85e8) = log(4.85e8+1) = 20.000000002. Same result. So our `if (x > 0) x + log1pf(expf(-x)) else log1pf(expf(x))` is stable and accurate. It matches the mathematical definition. PyTorch's implementation for `mish` likely computes `softplus` first, which is `log1p(exp(x))`. So the output should match within fp32 tolerance. We need to be careful about `tanhf`. CUDA `tanhf` is accurate. Potential issue: For negative large x (e.g., -20), `expf(x)` underflows to 0, `log1pf(0) = 0`. So sp=0. tanh(0)=0. mish = x * 0 = -0.0. In PyTorch, softplus(-20) = log1p(exp(-20)) ≈ exp(-20) ≈ 2e-9. tanh(2e-9) ≈ 2e-9. mish ≈ -20 * 2e-9 = -4e-8. Our code: since x<0, sp = log1pf(expf(x)). For x=-20, expf(-20)=2e-9, log1pf(2e-9)=2e-9. sp=2e-9. tanh(sp)=2e-9. mish = -20 * 2e-9 = -4e-8. So correct. Wait, earlier I said it would underflow to 0. expf(-20) is 2e-9, not underflow. expf(-103) underflows. So for very negative values (e.g., -100), expf(-100) underflows to 0, sp=0, mish=0. In PyTorch, exp(-100) would underflow to 0 in float too, so same. So fine. What about x = -0.0? `if (x > 0.0f)` is false (since -0.0 > 0 is false). Then `sp = log1pf(expf(-0.0)) = log1pf(1.0) = log(2) = 0.693...` Actually expf(-0.0) = 1.0. So sp = log1pf(1.0) = log(2). mish = -0.0 * tanhf(log(2)) = -0.0. In PyTorch, `mish(-0.0) = -0.0 * tanh(softplus(-0.0))`. softplus(-0.0) = log(1+1) = log(2). tanh(log(2)) ≈ 0.618. Product = -0.0. We get -0.0. That's okay. The sign of zero might not matter for tolerance. Another potential issue: For very large positive x, say x=50. `expf(-50)` underflows to 0, sp = 50 + 0 = 50. `tanhf(50)` returns 1.0f (since tanh of large number is 1). mish = 50. PyTorch might do the same. So fine. For x=90, `expf(-90)` underflows to 0, sp=90, tanhf(90)=1, mish=90. But if we used `log1pf(expf(x))` for x>0, `expf(90)` overflows to inf, `log1pf(inf)=inf`, `tanhf(inf)=1`, mish=90*1=90. But our branch avoids overflow. Good. Thus our mish implementation is solid. Let's write the Python module: ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline # Define CUDA code CUDA_SOURCE = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #define TILE_H 8 #define TILE_W 8 #define TILE_OC 16 #define KH 3 #define KW 3 __device__ __forceinline__ float mish(float x) { float sp; if (x > 0.0f) { sp = x + log1pf(expf(-x)); } else { sp = log1pf(expf(x)); } return x * tanhf(sp); } __global__ void fused_conv_mish_mish_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ bias, float* __restrict__ output, int N, int C_in, int H, int W, int C_out, int H_out, int W_out) { int num_oc_tiles = (C_out + TILE_OC - 1) / TILE_OC; int n = blockIdx.z / num_oc_tiles; int oc_tile = blockIdx.z % num_oc_tiles; int oc_base = oc_tile * TILE_OC; int oc = oc_base + threadIdx.z; int h_base = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int w_base = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int h_out = h_base + threadIdx.y; int w_out = w_base + threadIdx.x; bool valid = (n < N) && (oc < C_out) && (h_out < H_out) && (w_out < W_out); __shared__ float s_in[TILE_H + KH - 1][TILE_W + KW - 1]; __shared__ float s_w[KH][KW][TILE_OC]; int patchH = TILE_H + KH - 1; int patchW = TILE_W + KW - 1; int patchSize = patchH * patchW; int wTileSize = KH * KW * TILE_OC; float acc = 0.0f; const int tid = threadIdx.z * (TILE_H * TILE_W) + threadIdx.y * TILE_W + threadIdx.x; for (int c = 0; c < C_in; ++c) { // Load input tile for channel c if (tid < patchSize) { int pi = tid / patchW; int pj = tid % patchW; int h_in = h_base + pi; int w_in = w_base + pj; float val = 0.0f; if (h_in >= 0 && h_in < H && w_in >= 0 && w_in < W) { val = input[((n * C_in + c) * H + h_in) * W + w_in]; } s_in[pi][pj] = val; } // Load weights for output channels in tile if (tid < wTileSize) { int tz = tid % TILE_OC; int tky = (tid / TILE_OC) / KW; int tkx = (tid / TILE_OC) % KW; int oc_idx = oc_base + tz; float val = 0.0f; if (oc_idx < C_out) { val = weight[((oc_idx * C_in + c) * KH + tky) * KW + tkx]; } s_w[tky][tkx][tz] = val; } __syncthreads(); if (valid) { #pragma unroll for (int ky = 0; ky < KH; ++ky) { #pragma unroll for (int kx = 0; kx < KW; ++kx) { float iv = s_in[threadIdx.y + ky][threadIdx.x + kx]; float wv = s_w[ky][kx][threadIdx.z]; acc += iv * wv; } } } __syncthreads(); } if (valid) { acc += bias[oc]; float v = mish(acc); v = mish(v); output[((n * C_out + oc) * H_out + h_out) * W_out + w_out] = v; } } torch::Tensor fused_conv_mish_mish_forward( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias) { int N = input.size(0); int C_in = input.size(1); int H = input.size(2); int W = input.size(3); int C_out = weight.size(0); int KH_k = weight.size(2); int KW_k = weight.size(3); int H_out = H - KH_k + 1; int W_out = W - KW_k + 1; auto output = torch::empty({N, C_out, H_out, W_out}, input.options()); dim3 block(TILE_W, TILE_H, TILE_OC); int num_oc_tiles = (C_out + TILE_OC - 1) / TILE_OC; dim3 grid( (W_out + TILE_W - 1) / TILE_W, (H_out + TILE_H - 1) / TILE_H, N * num_oc_tiles ); fused_conv_mish_mish_kernel<<<grid, block>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), N, C_in, H, W, C_out, H_out, W_out ); return output; } ''' ``` Wait, we have a compile-time constant `KH` and `KW` in kernel but runtime `KH_k` and `KW_k` in host. Because we are reloading the input and weights many times across overlapping tiles! The input patch between adjacent spatial blocks overlaps by 2 pixels. The weights are reloaded for every spatial block and every batch. This is the weakness of tiling convolution naively. cuDNN solves this via im2col or Winograd, which reorganize data so that each input pixel is loaded exactly once (or few times) into shared memory, and weights are also loaded once. Grid-stride loop kernel: ```c++ __device__ __forceinline__ float softplus(float x) { if (x > 20.0f) return x; if (x < -20.0f) return expf(x); return log1pf(expf(x)); } __device__ __forceinline__ float mish(float x) { return x * tanhf(softplus(x)); } __device__ __forceinline__ float mish_mish(float x) { return mish(mish(x)); } __global__ void mish_mish_kernel(float* __restrict__ data, int64_t n) { int64_t idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int64_t stride = gridDim.x * blockDim.x; // process 4-element chunks int64_t n4 = n >> 2; float4* ptr4 = reinterpret_cast<float4*>(data); for (int64_t i = idx; i < n4; i += stride) { float4 v = ptr4[i]; v.x = mish_mish(v.x); v.y = mish_mish(v.y); v.z = mish_mish(v.z); v.w = mish_mish(v.w); ptr4[i] = v; } // tail int64_t tail_start = n4 << 2; for (int64_t i = tail_start + idx; i < n; i += stride) { data[i] = mish_mish(data[i]); } } ``` This is in-place. We need to ensure `data` pointer is aligned to 16 bytes. PyTorch tensors are aligned to at least 16 bytes, typically 32 or 64. We can align by checking `((uintptr_t)data % 16 == 0)`. Let me check. Actually, in ATen/native/cuda/Activation.cu: ```cpp template <typename scalar_t> __device__ __forceinline__ scalar_t mish(scalar_t x) { return x * tanh(softplus(x)); } ``` And softplus: ```cpp template <typename scalar_t> __device__ __forceinline__ scalar_t softplus(scalar_t x, scalar_t beta, scalar_t threshold) { scalar_t z = exp(x * beta); return (x * beta) > threshold ? x : log1p(z) / beta; } ``` For default beta=1.0 and threshold=20.0! So PyTorch's softplus threshold is 20.0! My if x > 20.0f return x matches PyTorch exactly! And for x < -20.0f, PyTorch computes exp(x) which underflows to 0, and log1p(0) = 0. My x < -20 branch returns exp(x) then multiplies by x in mish... wait no, mish uses softplus, not exp directly. For x < -20: PyTorch softplus(x) = log1p(exp(x)) ≈ exp(x) since exp(x) << 1. So softplus(x) ≈ exp(x). Then mish(x) = x * tanh(exp(x)) ≈ x * exp(x) because tanh(y) ≈ y for small y. Since x < -20, exp(x) < 2e-9, so mish(x) ≈ x * exp(x) which underflows to 0. My implementation: for x < -20, I return exp(x) in softplus, then mish = x * tanh(exp(x)). That's approximately x*exp(x), same as PyTorch. For x = -30, exp(-30) ~ 1e-13, tanh(1e-13) ~ 1e-13, mish ~ -3e-12. In PyTorch: softplus(-30) = log1p(exp(-30)) ≈ exp(-30) = 1e-13, tanh(1e-13) ≈ 1e-13, mish ≈ -3e-12. Very close. So exp(-30) won't underflow. softplus(-30) = log1p(exp(-30)) ≈ exp(-30) via linear approximation of log1p for small arguments? Here's my final kernel code: ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline import uuid CUDA_SOURCE = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cstdint> __device__ __forceinline__ float softplus(float x) { if (x > 20.0f) return x; if (x < -20.0f) return expf(x); return log1pf(expf(x)); } __device__ __forceinline__ float mish(float x) { return x * tanhf(softplus(x)); } __global__ void mish_mish_kernel(float* __restrict__ data, int64_t n) { int64_t idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int64_t stride = gridDim.x * blockDim.x; int64_t n4 = n >> 2; float4* ptr4 = reinterpret_cast<float4*>(data); for (int64_t i = idx; i < n4; i += stride) { float4 v = ptr4[i]; v.x = mish(mish(v.x)); v.y = mish(mish(v.y)); v.z = mish(mish(v.z)); v.w = mish(mish(v.w)); ptr4[i] = v; } int64_t tail_start = n4 << 2; for (int64_t i = tail_start + idx; i < n; i += stride) { data[i] = mish(mish(data[i])); } } void fused_mish_mish_forward(torch::Tensor input) { TORCH_CHECK(input.is_cuda(), "input must be a CUDA tensor"); TORCH_CHECK(input.scalar_type() == torch::kFloat32, "input must be float32"); TORCH_CHECK(input.is_contiguous(), "input must be contiguous"); int64_t n = input.numel(); if (n == 0) return; float* data = input.data_ptr<float>(); const int block_size = 512; int64_t num_blocks = (n + block_size - 1) / block_size; mish_mish_kernel<<<num_blocks, block_size>>>(data, n); } ''' CPP_SOURCES = r''' void fused_mish_mish_forward(torch::Tensor input); ''' unique_name = 'fused_mish_mish_' + uuid.uuid4().hex[:8] _fused_ext = load_inline( name=unique_name, cpp_sources=CPP_SOURCES, cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE, functions=['fused_mish_mish_forward'], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3'], verbose=False, ) class ModelNew(nn.Module): def __init__(self, in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size): super(ModelNew, self).__init__() self.conv = nn.Conv2d(in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size, bias=True) def forward(self, x): x = self.conv(x) # Apply two mish activations in a single fused in-place kernel, # avoiding two separate PyTorch kernels and saving memory bandwidth. _fused_ext.fused_mish_mish_forward(x) return x ``` Wait, but does this exactly match with `torch._C._GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI` issue? i < n4; i += stride) {\n float4 v = ptr_in[i];\n v.x = mish_mish(v.x);\n v.y = mish_mish(v.y);\n v.z = mish_mish(v.z);\n v.w = mish_mish(v.w);\n ptr_out[i] = v;\n }\n\n int64_t tail_start = n4 << 2;\n for (int64_t i = tail_start + idx; i < n; i += stride) {\n data[i] = mish_mish(data[i]);\n }\n}\n\nvoid launch_mish_mish(torch::Tensor input) {\n TORCH_CHECK(input.is_cuda(), \"input must be a CUDA tensor\");\n TORCH_CHECK(input.scalar_type() == torch::kFloat32, \"input must be float32\");\n TORCH_CHECK(input.is_contiguous(), \"input must be contiguous\");\n\n int64_t n = input.numel();\n if (n == 0) return;\n\n float* data = input.data_ptr<float>();\n const int block_size = 512;\n int64_t n4 = n >> 2;\n int64_t num_blocks = (n4 + block_size - 1) / block_size;\n mish_mish_kernel<<<num_blocks, block_size>>>(data, n);\n}\n'''\n\nCPP_SOURCES = r'''\nvoid launch_mish_mish(torch::Tensor input);\n'''\n\nabi_flag = '-D_GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI=1' if torch._C._GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI else '-D_GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI=0'\n\nunique_name = 'fused_mish_mish_' + uuid.uuid4().hex[:8]\n\n_fused_ext = load_inline(\n name=unique_name,\n cpp_sources=CPP_SOURCES,\n cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE,\n functions=['launch_mish_mish'],\n extra_cflags=[abi_flag],\n extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3', abi_flag],\n verbose=False,\n)\n\nclass ModelNew(nn.Module):\n def __init__(self, in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size):\n super(ModelNew, self).__init__()\n self.conv = nn.Conv2d(in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size, bias=True)\n\n def forward(self, x):\n x = self.conv(x)\n _fused_ext.launch_mish_mish(x)\n return x\n" }

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline
import uuid

CUDA_SOURCE = r'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <cstdint>

__device__ __forceinline__ float softplus(float x) {
    if (x > 20.0f) return x;
    if (x < -20.0f) return expf(x);
    return log1pf(expf(x));
}

__device__ __forceinline__ float mish_mish(float x) {
    float sp1 = softplus(x);
    float y = x * tanhf(sp1);
    float sp2 = softplus(y);
    return y * tanhf(sp2);
}

__global__ void mish_mish_kernel(float* __restrict__ data, int64_t n) {
    int64_t idx = static_cast<int64_t>(blockIdx.x) * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x;
    int64_t stride = static_cast<int64_t>(gridDim.x) * blockDim.x;

    int64_t n4 = n >> 2;
    float4* __restrict__ ptr4 = reinterpret_cast<float4*>(data);

    for (int64_t i = idx; i < n4; i += stride) {
        float4 v = ptr4[i];
        v.x = mish_mish(v.x);
        v.y = mish_mish(v.y);
        v.z = mish_mish(v.z);
        v.w = mish_mish(v.w);
        ptr4[i] = v;
    }

    int64_t tail_start = n4 << 2;
    for (int64_t i = tail_start + idx; i < n; i += stride) {
        data[i] = mish_mish(data[i]);
    }
}

void launch_mish_mish(torch::Tensor input) {
    TORCH_CHECK(input.is_cuda(), "input must be a CUDA tensor");
    TORCH_CHECK(input.scalar_type() == torch::kFloat32, "input must be float32");
    TORCH_CHECK(input.is_contiguous(), "input must be contiguous");

    int64_t n = input.numel();
    if (n == 0) return;

    float* data = input.data_ptr<float>();
    const int block_size = 512;
    int64_t n4 = n >> 2;
    int64_t num_blocks = (n4 + block_size - 1) / block_size;
    mish_mish_kernel<<<num_blocks, block_size>>>(data, n);
}
'''

CPP_SOURCES = r'''
void launch_mish_mish(torch::Tensor input);
'''

abi_flag = '-D_GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI=1' if torch._C._GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI else '-D_GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI=0'

unique_name = 'fused_mish_mish_' + uuid.uuid4().hex[:8]

_fused_ext = load_inline(
    name=unique_name,
    cpp_sources=CPP_SOURCES,
    cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE,
    functions=['launch_mish_mish'],
    extra_cflags=[abi_flag],
    extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3', abi_flag],
    verbose=False,
)

class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size):
        super(ModelNew, self).__init__()
        self.conv = nn.Conv2d(in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size, bias=True)

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.conv(x)
        _fused_ext.launch_mish_mish(x)
        return x
